        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;

          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }

        }

          flex-grow: 0;

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

function f(a,b) {



<span class="line"><!---->function f(a,b) {<!----></span>



<br>





	let t = a >= b;



<span class="line"><!---->	let t = a &gt;= b;<!----></span>



<br>





    	while (t != 0) {



<span class="line"><!---->    	while (t != 0) {<!----></span>



<br>





        	a = a | (b - a);



<span class="line"><!---->        	a = a | (b - a);<!----></span>



<br>





        	let unused = a >= b;



<span class="line"><!---->        	let unused = a &gt;= b;<!----></span>



<br>





		t = a < b;



<span class="line"><!---->		t = a &lt; b;<!----></span>



<br>





    	}



<span class="line"><!---->    	}<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>



<br>





function test() {



<span class="line"><!---->function test() {<!----></span>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->	f(Infinity,1);<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->	f(undefined, undefined);<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->%PrepareFunctionForOptimization(f);<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->test();<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->%OptimizeFunctionOnNextCall(test);<!----></span>

Labels

:

<strong><!---->Labels:</strong>


          


          

Type-Bug


          




          

<br>


        




        




      

<div class="issue-diff">
        <!---->
          <strong><!---->Labels:</strong>
          
          Type-Bug
          
          <br>
        <!---->
        
      </div>

<br>


    


        


      


        









After a longer investigation, I'm convinced that this is not a security bug, for a number of reasons:



<span class="line"><!---->After a longer investigation, I'm convinced that this is not a security bug, for a number of reasons:<!----></span>



<br>





1.) At the core of this issue, there is an inconsistency in the Turbofan graph, which this DCHECK is pointing out. However, the respective subgraph is unreachable in an actual execution, because every execution would already deoptimize before that point.



<span class="line"><!---->1.) At the core of this issue, there is an inconsistency in the Turbofan graph, which this DCHECK is pointing out. However, the respective subgraph is unreachable in an actual execution, because every execution would already deoptimize before that point.<!----></span>



<br>





2.) --assert-types seems to be required to produces this effect, which is an internal flag for testing.



<span class="line"><!---->2.) --assert-types seems to be required to produces this effect, which is an internal flag for testing.<!----></span>



<br>





3.) In release builds, this is caught by a CHECK in the deoptimizer.



<span class="line"><!---->3.) In release builds, this is caught by a CHECK in the deoptimizer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





A fix is work in progress.

The root cause of this issue is InstructionSelector::EmitIdentity, which renames uses of output operand by input operand. EmitIdentity is used by identity operations, for example bitcasts.



<span class="line"><!---->The root cause of this issue is InstructionSelector::EmitIdentity, which renames uses of output operand by input operand. EmitIdentity is used by identity operations, for example bitcasts.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Consider the following example, which is a slightly simplified subgraph produced by the above repro:



<span class="line"><!---->Consider the following example, which is a slightly simplified subgraph produced by the above repro:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





2: HeapConstant[0x... <undefined>]



<span class="line"><!---->2: HeapConstant[0x... &lt;undefined&gt;]<!----></span>



<br>





                        |



<span class="line"><!---->                        |<!----></span>



<br>





                        |



<span class="line"><!---->                        |<!----></span>



<br>





4: BitcastWord32ToWord64



<span class="line"><!---->4: BitcastWord32ToWord64<!----></span>



<br>





                        |



<span class="line"><!---->                        |<!----></span>



<br>





                        |



<span class="line"><!---->                        |<!----></span>



<br>





       6: TypedStateValues



<span class="line"><!---->       6: TypedStateValues<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





Notice, that the generated graph need not be reasonable, like in the example, where we basically treat a heap constant address as a smi value, because the graph may be the result of a speculative optimization that may be unreachable in any actual program execution.



<span class="line"><!---->Notice, that the generated graph need not be reasonable, like in the example, where we basically treat a heap constant address as a smi value, because the graph may be the result of a speculative optimization that may be unreachable in any actual program execution.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Now, in InstructionSelector::VisitNode, when we visit 2: HeapConstant, we emit a constant operand, say v1 = [constant:1].



<span class="line"><!---->Now, in InstructionSelector::VisitNode, when we visit 2: HeapConstant, we emit a constant operand, say v1 = [constant:1].<!----></span>



<br>





When we visit the TypedStateValues (as part of the Call using it), in OperandForDeopt, we look at the input and decide whether to use an immedate or a stack slot for this operand. A immediate would be used if the input was a HeapConstant, but since it is not, we use a StackSlot, so we emit a call



<span class="line"><!---->When we visit the TypedStateValues (as part of the Call using it), in OperandForDeopt, we look at the input and decide whether to use an immedate or a stack slot for this operand. A immediate would be used if the input was a HeapConstant, but since it is not, we use a StackSlot, so we emit a call<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





ArchCallCodeObject ...., v2, ....



<span class="line"><!---->ArchCallCodeObject ...., v2, ....<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





where this particular input v2 must be in a stack slot. As long as we generate an instruction for the operation in the middle, everything is fine, imagine:



<span class="line"><!---->where this particular input v2 must be in a stack slot. As long as we generate an instruction for the operation in the middle, everything is fine, imagine:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1: v1 = [constant:1]



<span class="line"><!---->1: v1 = [constant:1]<!----></span>



<br>





2: v2 = any_unary_op v1



<span class="line"><!---->2: v2 = any_unary_op v1<!----></span>



<br>





3: ArchCallCodeObject ...., v2, ....



<span class="line"><!---->3: ArchCallCodeObject ...., v2, ....<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Here, the live range of v1 and v2 span instructions 1-2 and 2-3, respectively, allowing the register allocator to assign a stack slot to v2 while keeping v1 in a register (constant operand is just a specialization of a register operand). Instruction 2 bridges the gap between those by consuming its input from the register and producing its output in a stack slot.



<span class="line"><!---->Here, the live range of v1 and v2 span instructions 1-2 and 2-3, respectively, allowing the register allocator to assign a stack slot to v2 while keeping v1 in a register (constant operand is just a specialization of a register operand). Instruction 2 bridges the gap between those by consuming its input from the register and producing its output in a stack slot.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The problem now rises when the any_unary_op instruction in the middle is a identity operation (e.g. BitcastWord32ToWord64), because instead of emitting any instruction, we InstructionSelector just performs renaming, ending in



<span class="line"><!---->The problem now rises when the any_unary_op instruction in the middle is a identity operation (e.g. BitcastWord32ToWord64), because instead of emitting any instruction, we InstructionSelector just performs renaming, ending in<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1: v1 = [constant:1]



<span class="line"><!---->1: v1 = [constant:1]<!----></span>



<br>





2: ArchCallCodeObject ...., v1, ....



<span class="line"><!---->2: ArchCallCodeObject ...., v1, ....<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





where now a (constant) register operand is assigned where a stack slot is expected. This causes the failure of the DCHECK in RegisterAllocator::ConvertUsesToOperand (and the CHECK faillure in the deoptimizer).



<span class="line"><!---->where now a (constant) register operand is assigned where a stack slot is expected. This causes the failure of the DCHECK in RegisterAllocator::ConvertUsesToOperand (and the CHECK faillure in the deoptimizer).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





A number of solutions are conceivable. The most robust I can think of right now is to change EmitIdentity such that is aware of the operand types and requirements (in addition to the MachineRepresentation, which is currently ignored as well and produces this related bug: 



<span class="line"><!---->A number of solutions are conceivable. The most robust I can think of right now is to change EmitIdentity such that is aware of the operand types and requirements (in addition to the MachineRepresentation, which is currently ignored as well and produces this related bug: <!----></span>





https://bugs.chromium.org/p/v8/issues/detail?id=10636



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/v8/issues/detail?id=10636"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/v8/issues/detail?id=10636<!----></a>





)



<span class="line"><!---->)<!----></span>





 and perform renaming only if this is actually sound.



<span class="line"><!----> and perform renaming only if this is actually sound.<!----></span>

Here is a prototype for a fix in the register allocator:



<span class="line"><!---->Here is a prototype for a fix in the register allocator:<!----></span>



<br>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/2563689



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/2563689"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/2563689<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





This generally allows virtual registers defined by a constant operand to have uses with MUST_HAVE_SLOT policy, and adds the missing gap moves before every such use. This was not supported before but I'm not sure if this was explicitly enforced anywhere in the previous phases, or if we just happened to never hit this case until now.



<span class="line"><!---->This generally allows virtual registers defined by a constant operand to have uses with MUST_HAVE_SLOT policy, and adds the missing gap moves before every such use. This was not supported before but I'm not sure if this was explicitly enforced anywhere in the previous phases, or if we just happened to never hit this case until now.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Two minor caveats:



<span class="line"><!---->Two minor caveats:<!----></span>



<br>





- Adds an extra pointer field for each vreg (TopLevelLiveRange),



<span class="line"><!---->- Adds an extra pointer field for each vreg (TopLevelLiveRange),<!----></span>



<br>





- Does not find a good spill position, instead a gap move is added for each use requiring it, following the logic of fixed-slot constraints. This should be fine since this case seems very rare



<span class="line"><!---->- Does not find a good spill position, instead a gap move is added for each use requiring it, following the logic of fixed-slot constraints. This should be fine since this case seems very rare<!----></span>

[regalloc] Fix slot requirement for live ranges defined by a const



<span class="line"><!---->[regalloc] Fix slot requirement for live ranges defined by a const<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Live ranges defined by a constant operand normally don't require a spill



<span class="line"><!---->Live ranges defined by a constant operand normally don't require a spill<!----></span>



<br>





slot since they can just rematerialize the value from the constant. In



<span class="line"><!---->slot since they can just rematerialize the value from the constant. In<!----></span>



<br>





the attached issue however, deoptimization adds an explicit slot



<span class="line"><!---->the attached issue however, deoptimization adds an explicit slot<!----></span>



<br>





requirement for a range that is defined by a constant operand. This case



<span class="line"><!---->requirement for a range that is defined by a constant operand. This case<!----></span>



<br>





is not expected in the register allocator and we eventually hit a



<span class="line"><!---->is not expected in the register allocator and we eventually hit a<!----></span>



<br>





DCHECK.



<span class="line"><!---->DCHECK.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This fix allocates a new stack slot during the MeetRegisterConstraints



<span class="line"><!---->This fix allocates a new stack slot during the MeetRegisterConstraints<!----></span>



<br>





and adds the missing gap move.



<span class="line"><!---->and adds the missing gap move.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Drive-by: remove dead method LiveRange::NextSlotPosition.



<span class="line"><!---->Drive-by: remove dead method LiveRange::NextSlotPosition.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<input id="targetProjectInput" aria-owns="chops-autocomplete-1" aria-autocomplete="both" aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="listbox" aria-activedescendant="">


              




      


        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
